## ענינים כלליים

## 160

### General Matters

...Regarding his question in the holy letter of Cheshvan 5705, which was omitted (in the copy of *Sefer Sichos* 5702, chapter 6) from the list of the "three great forces": *a fire infolding itself*. The intent of the copyist was that the "three great forces" are: wind, storm, and a great cloud.

Now, although one can find a basis for interpreting "wind" and "storm" as a single entity—based on what is written in *Avodas HaKodesh* (cited in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Kedoshim*, section *Shir HaShirim*, ch. 19), and in *Zohar* III, 196a, that "wind-storm" refers to *Zon* (Ze'er Anpin and Nukvah), whereas "wind" alone or "storm" alone [refers to something else]—this is merely for the sake of pilpul. It is simple that the omission in the printed text is a mistake. It should read: "wind, storm, a great cloud, and a fire infolding itself."

See *Etz Chaim*, Gate 7, ch. 3, and *Likutei Torah*, discourse *Vayikchu Eilecha Parah*, which discuss the matter of chapter 6 of *Sefer Sichos* 5702, where "fire" is also explicitly mentioned.

Furthermore, there are many places in general where "a fire infolding itself" is counted among the list of the *kelipos* (for example, *Zohar* III, 131a).

However, it is seemingly difficult to understand why *Sefer Sichos* 5702 lists and explains "wind-storm" and "a great cloud," while "a fire infolding itself" is mentioned only by way of allusion in the word "etc." (*v'go*), especially since it is known how precise the Alter Rebbe was in the language of his *Sefer Sichos*. In all the editions of *Tanya* that I have seen, including those printed during the Alter Rebbe’s lifetime, it is written as mentioned above.

Simply put, it could be said: Are we to act like a peddler and count every detail? An allusion is sufficient.

And the reason it explains "a great cloud" and does not write "wind-storm, etc." is because the language of the verse is: "a wind-storm came out of the north, a great cloud, and a fire infolding itself, and a brightness was round about it." If it had written in *Sefer Sichos* "wind-storm, etc.," there would be room to err that the "north" is one of the "three great forces." But the "etc." that follows "a great cloud" cannot be mistaken in its intent. Moreover, the words "a fire infolding itself" are adjacent to the words "a great cloud."

—And were I not afraid, I would say that in *Sefer Sichos* it should read "cloud" (*anan*) without the *vav*, as in the language of the verse, and as it begins "and they are called..." to which "cloud" without a *vav* corresponds later. But in all the editions, it is with a *vav*—

One must also understand the intent of what is written in *Sefer Sichos*: "and they are called in the Chariot, etc.," for seemingly, what is the practical difference here? It could be said that it comes to indicate from where the "three great forces" (and also the "three impure ones") emerged, since there is no good in them at all (see this at length in *Likutei Torah*, *L'Gimmel Parshiyos*, discourse *Lehavin Inyan HaBrachos*, sections 7-8). Regarding this, it says "and they are called, etc.," which is their root above.

—See the explanation of *Eileh Masei* 3 at its beginning. —This was not said earlier in chapter 1, because there the "three great forces" were mentioned only incidentally.

While speaking on this subject, I would like to note that for the time being, I have not found in *Chassidus* an explanation of the distinction between the "three great forces" themselves, one from the other, except for the general distinction in the aforementioned explanation of *Eileh Masei*.

## 161

At first glance, it can be said that they are in three lines (three elements: fire, wind, and cloud—which is water—and the element of earth is included in them, as is known). The right line in the powers of the soul is water, the left is fire, and the middle is wind.

Regarding the path of *mussar* and *avodah*, their matter is explained in *Rosh Chodesh*, discourse *HaYirah*, ch. 4. In *Pardes*, Gate 26, ch. 7, it is explained—based on *Tikkunei Zohar*—that cloud, fire, and wind are *Chadar* (an acronym for *Chochma, Da'as, Ruach*). In *Koheles Yaakov*, under the entries for fire, cloud, and wind, they are *Binah* and *Zon* of the *kelipah*—based on the introduction to *Tikkunei Zohar* that the letters *Heh-Vav-Heh* of the Name are embedded in them—and under the entry for the four *kelipos*, which are *Chagas, Nehi, Malchus* of the *kelipah*, and the "three impure ones" are *Ein Sof* and *Chachmah-Binah* of the *kelipah*, etc. If so, according to what is explained in the discourse *B'Yom HaShemini Atzeres* 5730 and the discourse *Lo Tilbash Shatnez* 5728 (and see *Etz Chaim*, Gate 48, ch. 3; *Mevo Shearim*, Gate 6, part 2, ch. 4), in the *kelipah*, the order is reversed: *Malchus* and below it *Ze'er Anpin*, etc. According to this, "a fire infolding itself" is below wind and cloud, which is difficult to reconcile with the aforementioned *Likutei Torah* on *Masei*. And in *Etz Chaim*, Gate 47, ch. 4, it is implied that their order from above to below is wind-storm, cloud, and fire.

See also what is written regarding the third *kelipah* in the nut (which is fire) in *Zohar* III, 287a and 287b—cited in *Pardes* there, ch. 26—and in *Pri Etz Chaim*, Gate of Purim, near the end. But this is not the place to elaborate...
[quotation](From a letter, Chanukah 5703)[/quotation]

We were happy to hear from... that he is among the founders of the *Tehillim* society in the synagogue...

Fortunate is he who has merited such a great thing and has a share in the merit of all those who recite *Tehillim* in public in this society. Surely he goes from strength to strength and strives, together with all those assisting him, to influence all the congregants in his synagogue to register for this *Tehillim* society.

Surely he knows what the *Tzemach Tzedek* said: "If you knew the power of the verses of *Tehillim* and their effect in the highest heavens, you would recite them at all times. Know that the chapters of *Tehillim* break through all barriers and ascend from elevation to elevation without any hindrance, and they prostrate themselves before the Master of the World and accomplish their work with kindness and mercy."

We enclose herewith a letter from the Rebbe *shlita* regarding the recitation of *Tehillim* and a letter from *Machne Israel* regarding the global *Tehillim* society, and we hope that the *Tehillim* society managed by... will also see fit to register with the global *Tehillim* society.

## 162

May the merit of reciting *Tehillim* stand for him and for all his members in the *Tehillim* society in the synagogue... to be saved from the birth pangs of *Moshiach* and to merit receiving the face of *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* very, very soon.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah*, immediate *geulah*.
[quotation](From a letter, 25 Cheshvan 5705)[/quotation]

...And here, for a *Ben Noach*, only a missing limb disqualifies. For a *Ben Noach* and a *Ben Yisrael*, the distinction was made through the Giving of the Torah, whose matter is the nullification of the decree that "the children of Rome shall not descend, etc.," but rather that heaven and earth were made into one. In terms of subtlety, this is the innovation of the teachings of *Chassidus*: there is nothing else, *Daled* (G-d) is one from above to below and from below to above. And this is why for a *Ben Noach* only a missing limb—the total absence of the *mitzvah*—disqualifies, whereas for *Chassidim*, many matters—blemishes—disqualify, [as well as] the beautification of the *mitzvah*. And in general, *Elokim* (G-d) in *gematria* is *HaTeva* (nature), and in *gematria* is *mum* (blemish), and it must be that *Bara Elokim* (G-d created) is to heal nature.
[quotation](From a letter, 8 Tishrei 5703)[/quotation]

In response to your letter of Thursday, which concludes with twelve questions, and you write that there is more to ask, but there is no end to speech.

Aside from the fact that one can answer such twelve questions not in a letter, the main point is that when you answer these twelve, the *yetzer* will present others in their place, and likely even greater in number.

The main thing is that for a *bochur* of your age, it is not the matter to search for questions and to think that the reason you have not received an answer to all the questions is the reason for the lack of *hasmadah* (diligence) and *shekidah* (assiduity). The matter of a *yeshiva bochur* in general is to study Torah and to desire to understand what is written in it, and not at all to "dig" (*gribelen*)—perhaps one can innovate a difficulty that others have not stood upon, and to investigate who can resolve it.

For example, like someone who begins to study the science of medicine, *l'havdil*, and the day after the beginning, he informs his teachers that they must explain to him why, when they cure this and that, they give bitter pills—perhaps the pills could be sweet; why do they need to perform surgery, let them heal without surgery, etc., and the like. And regardless of the fact that you write that you have already been studying in *yeshiva* for two years, regarding the depth that exists in our holy Torah, this is perhaps further away than the knowledge of the beginner studying the science of medicine on the first day, compared to the knowledge of a doctor who has finished.

It is understood that I do not mean to say that one should not understand what is written in the Torah; on the contrary, it is an obligation to study Torah in a manner and specifically to understand it. But there must be the precedence of *na'aseh* (we will do) to *nishma* (we will hear), a matter of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke), for then one does not allow oneself to be confused by the *yetzer* from studying Torah with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*. And then, even if there is some difficulty, it does not affect the *hasmadah* and *shekidah*. Especially when you go over the twelve difficulties again, as you write yourself at the beginning of your letter, these are matters that surely the great men of Israel have stood upon, and we know that they studied Torah with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* and fulfilled *mitzvos* with the greatest beauty. From this, it is understood: a) that there is a satisfying answer, b) and if there is a detail that is not fully understood in the intellect, it does not touch at all upon the conduct of how a Jew needs to conduct himself according to the Torah. For what is the wonder that a human does not understand what the Holy One, Blessed be He, understands, *kivayachol*? On the contrary, the wonder is the opposite: that there are matters of the wisdom and will of the Holy One, Blessed be He, which is the Torah, that a human who is a limited being understands with his limited intellect.

May it be the will that you leave the path of "digging" (*gribelen zich*) and searching for questions, which is not at all your matter, and give yourself to fulfill the statement of the *Mishnah*: "I was created to serve my Maker." Especially as we approach the time of the Giving of our Torah, which, as mentioned above, they received through the precedence of *na'aseh* to *nishma*, and as our Sages of blessed memory said, that it must specifically be so, for then "the integrity of the upright shall guide them," and if otherwise, *chas v'shalom*, etc. (see *Maseches Shabbos* 88a).

With blessings for good tidings.
[quotation](From a letter, 27 Iyar 5717)[/quotation]

I received your letter of Tuesday, and thank you for the pleasantness of your writing regarding your impression of my letter, etc., and in your words: "a good feeling to know that there exists a partnership of fate and mutual responsibility between the members of our people wherever they are."

My hope is that you know that the teachings of *Chassidus* add an essential addition to this: that all the members of our people wherever they are are not only partners in their matters—for partnership means that two separate people participate in one matter—but rather, in the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, founder of the *Chabad* *Chassidic* teachings, they are "one complete stature, etc., that they all gather together to be made one."

## 166

And each and every one of us will do everything mentioned with vitality and enthusiasm, appropriate to the magnitude of the value of the task and in a manner as the instruction of the coming days of Chanukah, and the Chanukah candle, which we light, "increases and goes on," increasing in light from day to day.

With respect and blessing.
[quotation](From a letter, 11 Kislev 5734)[/quotation]

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of Friday, 6 Sivan, which reached me after a long delay.

Contrary to the usual order, I will begin from its conclusion, in your words: "I am not religious-believing," etc. And I note what is stated in quotation marks, so as not to stumble into the grave sin of slandering a person from the children of Israel, whom the Torah of Truth testifies are "believers, the children of believers," as is explicit in several places in the Torah, starting even from the time they were in the harsh exile in the land of Egypt, "the nakedness of the land" (*Shabbos* 97a, cited in Rashi’s commentary on the Torah), and all the more so after the Giving of the Torah, when the Holy One, Blessed be He, Creator of the world and its Guide, established: "And you shall be unto Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation."

But since the Holy One, Blessed be He, wanted that every individual of Israel, who belongs to a wise and understanding people, should do the good and the upright from his own good will and not be forced into it, therefore He gave each one free choice: "See, I have set before you this day life and the good, etc., and you shall choose life." But a Jew cannot change his essentiality and his true nature. Rather, sometimes due to various reasons, it remains in his inwardness, and the habit which becomes a second nature covers his true nature, until his eyes are blinded from seeing the matters in their truth. And to what is this comparable? To a person who was created with beautiful eyes (and in the language of the verse: "Your eyes are like doves," like this dove that recognizes and clings to its mate). But he was also given the possibility to insert colored lenses into them, and the one who sees with fleshly eyes does not distinguish if this is the color of his eyes or the color of the lens, and when the lenses are ugly, he also sees the whole world in a distorted manner.

And the explanation of the Rambam is known, the *Guide for the Perplexed* of his generation and for these generations, that every Jewish person truly wants to fulfill all that is commanded upon him, but sometimes "his *yetzer* forces him," and when the confusion of the *yetzer* is nullified, in whatever matter it may be, the essence and the true nature and his true will are revealed (see Rambam, *Hilchos Geirushin*, end of ch. 2).

And in this is also the answer to your letter that it is difficult for you to keep and be careful with the *halachos*, or that it seems to you that you fulfill them out of fear, etc.—these are nothing but the enticements of the *yetzer* and imaginations that have no substance. And when you overcome them, you will see that, on the contrary, you are a believer, the child of a believer, and you serve G-d in accordance with what is written: "And you shall love the L-rd your G-d, etc.," "And you shall teach them to your children, etc.," "And you shall bind them for a sign upon your hand, etc."

If you write your name and your mother's name, as we mention in prayer, I will mention you for a blessing from G-d in the content of your letter, including also to serve G-d out of tranquility of the soul and tranquility of the body, and as we are commanded—out of joy, and also out of expansion in the literal sense.

With respect and blessing.
[quotation](From a letter, 27 Sivan 5740)[/quotation]

...Regarding what you wrote about... *shiyeh*, that all the letters to speak with him have already been exhausted, the contradiction is understood from what you conclude afterwards, that in his words he still stands. For since there is no truth but Torah and its instructions, and one of its instructions is also known that every Jewish person wants to fulfill what is stated in the Torah, but there are those whose *yetzer hara* forces them (and therefore *kefiyah*—coercion—is effective, since it is only the removal of the force), and *kefiyah*, sometimes, is much stronger in words than in another manner, and it is obvious that it is more pleasant. As long as there is no movement in his position of the aforementioned, this is proven evidence—that they have not yet spoken with him, meaning to him. And the *mitzvah* of "You shall surely rebuke" was explained by our Sages that it is to the point of scolding, to the point of cursing, and to the point of striking. And the above is according to the law in the revealed Torah, and all the more so beyond the letter of the law and according to the inner dimension of the Torah. And it is famous—that, ultimately, "no one shall be cast away from Him." Especially as the end of the exile draws near and it must be that "all are righteous." And the interpretation of this is known, that the evil is separated from the good to one side, "all are righteous, etc."—surely one must act upon the aforementioned...
[quotation](From a letter, 4 Nissan 5718)[/quotation]

...To your writing that "I come from a secular family"—surely the "secularity" is a side effect and an external "garment" that covers the essence and the core that is found in him—for every one (and every woman) from his family *shiyeh* is a child of Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob (and a daughter of Sarah, Rebecca, Rachel, and Leah)

## 168

And after them—tens of generations of observers of Torah and *mitzvos*. It is just that G-d gave man the choice regarding his conduct, but it is not at all in his power to change his essence, his core, and his inwardness.
[quotation](From a letter, eve of Rosh Chodesh Mar-Cheshvan 5738)[/quotation]

In response to your two letters, in which you write the main points of your life, your state of mind, and your situation in general in the recent time, etc.

In general, there is no wonder in the lack of inner tranquility in a Jewish man or woman if their daily conduct does not correspond to their inner and essential nature, that is to say, corresponds to what is stated in our holy Torah regarding each and every one of the members of our people: "You are children to the L-rd your G-d." For if regarding a regular child he must conduct himself in a manner appropriate to his parents, all the more so and to an infinite degree regarding the children of the Place, the sons and daughters of Israel, whose Father in heaven taught them their path in life through His Torah (the word *hora'ah*—instruction), which is called "Torah of Life," and is He not also the Creator who created them in a manner appropriate to this life? Therefore, a disturbance in the aforementioned conduct brings a disturbance in the inner tranquility, etc.

From the above, the main advice for correcting the situation is also understood, and it is that first and foremost you must conduct yourself from now on in a manner appropriate to the will of G-d, the Creator of man and his Guide, as detailed in the *Shulchan Aruch*.

It is understood that I imagine there are those who challenge the aforementioned assumption from the reality that many of those who do not fulfill the *mitzvos* and despite this, it seems they lack nothing, not even regarding tranquility of the soul, etc. And the answer to the difficulty is also simple: a) In the style of our Sages—no person knows what is in the heart of his fellow, especially in areas that for several understandable reasons his fellow does not want to reveal to others. b) Like the illnesses of the body, *r"l*, which when the sick person does not feel that he is sick, this is not a sign of health, but on the contrary, a sign that the illness is heavy upon him. And in this manner, and even more so, it is regarding the state of health of the soul.

To your question regarding practical advice, etc., according to the description in your letter, you must begin to organize your life in a manner that you will get used to an organized life day by day, which will make it easier for you to enter into a fixed path of life, self-discipline, brain and intellect ruling over the heart and emotion, etc.

It is understood that there is no negation of what was written at the beginning of the letter in the above, but rather within this framework itself, a person must act in the way of nature. And as it seems from the main factors in your situation, it is the lack of

## 169

order and instability in your life in its external aspect, and as a result of this, also in the state of your soul, emotions, etc.

Since after a long time of an unorganized life it is difficult to get used to an organized and stable life, one of the ways to facilitate the aforementioned transition is through an external factor, I mean accepting a position and the like, that you will know that you have obligations toward others in a fixed job and fixed hours, etc.

It seems between the lines in your letter that you evaluate your situation as having hidden and serious reasons, etc. But in my opinion, the main point and the main factor are the two aforementioned matters: conduct according to the Torah and living in an organized order. And when you correct (slowly, at least) the aforementioned, your situation will improve to the most important degree, and perhaps even to the point of complete correction.

Another point in the above, and it is also essential, is a suitable *shidduch*. But it is simple that an approach to this important problem, all the more so a decision in this, must be out of tranquility of the soul and without confusion. Therefore, priority to organizing the first two matters, and after that to approach and take interest in the last point.

It is difficult to estimate in advance how much time will be needed for the aforementioned correction, but it is clear in my opinion that this depends only and solely on your will and your firm decision that you must go in the aforementioned direction, and after that to fulfill this decision without hesitations and doubts, etc.

May it be the will that the Almighty, who watches over each and every one with Divine Providence, will illuminate your path in life and cause you to succeed in all that you need in the physical and in the spiritual.

With blessings for health of the soul and health of the body and for good tidings.
[quotation](From a letter, 25 Tammuz 5726)[/quotation]

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your son... *shiyeh* and his place of study.

And it is simple, that true tranquility of the soul and a standing in life without tears and complications,

## 170

were important at all times and in all places, important beyond comparison to education and money, etc., all the more so in our era full of revolutions, etc., etc. And it is also simple that the period of education at the aforementioned age leaves its mark on many years after that, and this is not a matter of only those months that are found in a certain framework, but rather and essentially regarding the influence after it.

A common mistake among parents regarding the education of their children *shiyeh* is that their hope is that the state of the sons will be in a certain manner and at a certain level when they grow up and become independent, they limit the education in the days of childhood and youth to that measure and to that level, without paying attention that when the desire is that when the son is independent he will be at a certain level, then one must educate him at the age of education in a manner that after the influence of the street, etc., etc., will diminish the achievements of the education, that same level will remain, for which they hope.

In other words, regarding Torah and its *mitzvos* and Judaism in general, when they want that when the son is at the age of twenty or thirty he will be at a certain level of Judaism, fear of Heaven, etc., then at the age of thirteen to fifteen and taking into account the atmosphere from the outside, his level must be much higher.

But my hope is that since both of you, she and her husband *shiyeh*, are engaged in the field of education, you will take into account the aforementioned calculation, and will not be afraid of the immediate conclusions, for then surely you too will reach the same total, that his conclusion is in the manner of that telegram, and since surely only the true benefit of their son *shiyeh* is before your eyes, and not a matter of a theoretical system and worldview that must be realized in life without taking into account the results, etc., you will do as mentioned in the telegram out of will and joy.

And the days are days of awakening, and in the language of *Chassidus*, days of *is'arusa d'le'eila* (awakening from above).

With respect and with a blessing for a good writing and sealing.

## 171

Light and Torah of Truth because it illuminates matters in their truth, says and emphasizes clearly that the aforementioned connection is through daily conduct according to the will of the Creator and the keeping of His *mitzvos* that He commanded us in His Torah, as they are concentrated in the *Shulchan Aruch*.

Another foundation in our Torah is that the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not ask except according to the strength of the person, that is to say, that it is in the hand of each and every one to conduct himself according to His will as mentioned above despite all that was in the past, and the matter depends only on the true will and decision of the person. [quotation](From a letter, 2 Tammuz 5744)[/quotation]

After the longest break, your letter of 4/12 was received, in which you write about your state of mind now and your conduct which does not correspond to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of Life, as understood also in the literal sense, true life worthy of its name in our world, this physical world, and you justify your aforementioned conduct by the fact that so-and-so conducts himself not in order and also so-and-so is not in order, etc.

And the wonder is understood at this justification, for he is an adult for several years and wants to understand his matter and what pertains to him, and how is it that one justifies doing damage to oneself by the fact that so-and-so or his friend also damages himself.

To your question why this state happened to you—there is no wonder at all, when one changes the environment from one extreme to the other, and the change makes an impression, for it is a natural thing, even in matters of "sit and do not do," and especially when the good and upright path requires action, and sometimes also effort, and the main thing is that the opposite path is, as the words of the wise man: "The lips of a strange woman drip honey, and her end is bitter as wormwood," it is more comfortable to be drawn after the beginning which is in the present, not to restrain the *yetzer*, the will, and the desire, etc., than to strive to restrain and to hold back on the basis of the end that will be tomorrow.

And to your writing that at the time that you conducted yourself according to the Torah and the *mitzvah*, it was not with full awareness—here

## 172

in natural matters the emphasis is not on the awareness but on the conduct in practice in order to show the essence of his existence, evidence of the aforementioned, I mean, that the change of conduct because the new path is easier for the moment, and it is only that sometimes the full awareness that its end is bitter is confused, that the change is not only regarding matters of the holy Torah but also regarding matters that destroy the health of the body, and which every doctor will say absolutely, that this is against common sense and against human feeling, etc., and yet he weakens in them and perhaps even more, and surely to this there is no connection to the conduct of so-and-so between man and the Place, etc., but rather as mentioned above that it is easier not to restrain oneself than to restrain.

And when he will contemplate the truth of the matter in the aforementioned change, surely he will admit the reasons for the change, and may it be the will that from this he will draw the immediate conclusion, that it is the duty of a person as he is a person to live his life as a person and not as an animal, *r"l*, and the distinction is, that a person can rule over his spirit, and in the language of *Chassidus*, that the brain will be ruling over the heart, whereas the animal in the person, i.e., the animal soul, and *kal* (it is understood).

From the above it is understood that what you write at the end of your letter the epithets that I should call you, is not appropriate at all, and the epithet that I will call you, and my hope is strong only for a short period, is, that for the time being he has fallen under the influence of the *yetzer*, and has not yet recovered to fight against it, and to explain to himself, that in the creation the category of the inanimate is more (in quantity) than the category of the plant, and the plant more than the category of the animal, and the animal more than the category of the speaker, and in the species of the speaker, the people, the savage nations are the majority in quantity compared to those called enlightened, and the people of Israel is the fewest of all the nations from the time we became a people at the standing at Mount Sinai, and among the children of Israel themselves, those who observe Torah and *mitzvos* and live their lives according to them in completeness for the time being at least, *b'avonoseinu harabim*, do not constitute the majority, and as it is the opposite of nature that a person will say that he wants to live the life of an animal, plant, and inanimate because they are the majority in quantity, and in this manner it is in every stage and stage of all of them.

And further to add that we were promised, "no one shall be cast away from Him," and the saying of the Rebbe *Rayatz* is known in this that a Jew must be *a kluger* (wise) and surely ultimately they will place him in a standing and state appropriate to him, appropriate to his soul which is a part of G-d from above literally, until even at the time of the sin it was in faith with him, here he will strive with all his ability to explain this to himself, and in other words without extra complications and without unnecessary debate at all, and as the words of our Sages in their *Mishnah*, the action is the main thing.

And as we are found between *geulah* and *geulah*, 19 Kislev and the eve of the days of Chanukah, may it be the will that the change will begin in the aforementioned direction immediately and in a manner of "increasing and going on," increasing in light, and as the instruction of the days of Chanukah at the opening of his house from the outside and even from the outside, and increasing in them from day to day and from night to night.

Waiting for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

My opinion is that the situation has changed since the time when the custom of drinking *mashkeh* in abundance was prevalent, due to two factors: 1) The strength has already been given to *Anash* through the many accessible *maamarim* and *sichos* on matters of explanation and understanding, to influence the listeners without them needing *mashkeh* in abundance; the little that is used is sufficient. 2) Since in recent times, in particular, we are required with extra emphasis to engage in *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward), the matter of abundance in *mashkeh* is liable to distract from this greatly, which was not as relevant when the spreading was confined to the "four cubits" of the Chassidim and *Anash* alone. I was supported in point (1) by what I once heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in Riga, when he said, "I am now..."


## בהעלותך

## 192

### Beha'aloscha

In *Torah Ohr*, in the *maamar* beginning "On the 25th of Kislev," it states: "In the evening, he would light all seven candles, and in the morning, at the time of the *hatavas* (trimming) of the candles, he would light the sixth candle after its trimming, and afterwards he would light the seventh candle." Was this the order?

Seemingly, there is a further difficulty: at the beginning of the *drush*, it is written twice that during the day he would only light the sixth candle.

However, this *drush* is also printed in *Ohr HaTorah* with these three [candles], and it is evident there that this is not a scribal error.

There are several opinions regarding the order of the *hatavas* and the lighting of the candles. This *drush* follows the opinion that the Menorah was placed [in the *Heichal*] in a way that the candles were arranged "east to west" (*motza u-ma'arava*), and as stated there, the western candle is the sixth candle (unlike the opinion that it was placed "north to south" (*tzafon u-darom*), where the western candle is the middle candle, as found in *Menachos 98b*). This follows the explanation of the Rashba (in *Responsa*, *Siman* 79) and the Ramban (*Shabbos 22b* and his commentary on the Torah, *Shemos 27:20*), who explain that according to the opinion that it was placed "east to west" (and according to the view of the *Shas* in *Yoma*—which is the view being discussed here—that it disagrees with the *Mishnah* in *Tamid*, according to the Rashba), they would light two eastern candles during the day. Seemingly, the opinion of the *Tosafos* in *Yoma* (71a) is also this way. See also *Tosafos* in *Menachos* (86b) at the end: "And perhaps that which they instituted, etc." — and in any case, one must say that the *Tosafos* in *Yoma* disagrees with the *Tosafos* in *Menachos* regarding the *Perush HaMishnayos* of *Tamid*.

One should not raise the objection that if so, what is the *Tosafos* in *Yoma* struggling with by saying that this *Mishnah* was taught in the days of Shimon HaTzaddik, since even afterwards they would light two candles all day, and if so, he would have had to trim the candles—in the plural? Rather, it must be that they hold that only one candle was lit when the miracle ceased.

For one could say that according to all opinions, the western candle was lit in the morning, and nevertheless, it is not mentioned anywhere that the western candle is different from the other candles in that one is obligated to trim it twice a day (and see the aforementioned *Responsa* of the Rashba). Therefore, there is no obligation for a second trimming, and one may light it with an old wick or the like. If so, one can say the same regarding the two candles according to *Tosafos*. Thus, they resolve that this was during the time of the miracle, when they burned without interruption from evening to evening.

It follows simply that because the miracle occurred specifically with two candles, they were compelled to light—when the miracle ceased—two candles as well, like the aforementioned Ramban and Rashba.

One should not object that the *Rambam* (*Hilchos Beis HaBechirah* 3:12, 8) rules according to the opinion that it was placed "north to south." Firstly, *Ohr HaTorah* is not a book of *piskei dinim* (halachic rulings), and just as it explains here the order according to Abba Shaul, even though the *halacha* is according to the Sages (*Hilchos Temidin U-Musafin* 6:3, 4; and see *Ohr HaTorah* on this *drush*, end of section 2). Furthermore, there are those who disagree with the *Rambam* on this (see the *Hassagos* of the Ra'avad), and many have questioned this ruling, but this is not the place to elaborate.

The fact that at the beginning of the *drush* it is written that he would only light the sixth candle during the day is because there is no obligation

## 193

to light the seventh candle *per se*; it is only so that the western candle should be [the one] on the sixth candle, as stated in the aforementioned. This is exactly the language of the text, *Toras Kohanim*, *Shas*, etc., where everywhere it only speaks of one candle alone, except that the *Tanna* in *Tamid* (end of chapter 3) revealed that, by necessity, one must also light the candle that is to its east, and this is simple.

One should also note the language of the *drush* that the order was: trimming the seventh, then the sixth, and lighting the sixth, then the seventh. The reason is that when he enters the *Heichal* to fulfill the *hatavas* of the two candles, he encounters the seventh first, and we do not pass over *mitzvos*, so he trims it (see *Rashi* *s.v.* [and with it he would finish], *Shabbos 22b*)—and the *mitzvah* of trimming is equal for the sixth and seventh candles.

The order of lighting them in reverse can be explained:
1) When he finishes the *mitzvah* of trimming, he is standing by the sixth candle, and therefore he lights it first. One should not mix the two obligations of trimming and lighting.
2) The obligation of lighting during the day is only for the sixth candle, as the verse refers to it to "bring up the light." The lighting of the seventh is to reveal retroactively that the sixth candle is the western candle, and therefore he fulfills the essence of the *mitzvah* first.
3) We learn from the verse that the western candle was established to light the other candles from it, and therefore in the morning as well, we are careful to do so, even though the primary teaching is regarding the evening (*Tamid 6a*).

(From a letter, 9 Adar, '99)

The fact that it is written in *Likkutei Torah* at the beginning of *Beha'aloscha* that Aharon is one of the "seven shepherds"—this is somewhat of a contradiction to the *Gemara*, but it does not affect the *Tanya*. This has already been discussed in other places.

Regarding certain matters, but not the aforementioned, for Moshe is the totality of them all, as stated in the *Yerushalmi* (*Sanhedrin* 10, end of *halacha* 5): "There is no shepherd but Moshe."

(From a response, 7 Menachem Av, 5716)

## 194

After the longest silence, your letter from *Pesach Sheni* was received, which is the midpoint between the first *Pesach* and the time of the giving of our Torah in the course of the true redemption. For on the first *Pesach*, *chametz* is forbidden even in the smallest amount; on the festival of *Shavuos*, the two loaves—*chametz*—are baked, a *mitzvah* from the Torah; and on *Pesach Sheni*, *chametz* and *matzah* are together in the house—*matzah* is an obligation, *chametz* is permitted. It is the midpoint between the two matters, as is also understood from the holy *Zohar*, Part 2, 183b...

(From a letter, 18 Sivan, 5719)

... When you see... please convey my regards to him, and also convey to him what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, said—which is based on the well-known principle that from every single matter one must learn a moral lesson in the service of Hashem. The lesson from *Pesach Sheni* is that *es iz keinmol nit farfallen* (nothing is ever lost). Even if at the time when all of Israel were offering the *Pesach* sacrifice, one was impure or on a distant journey—or "for you," meaning it was of his own free will—nevertheless, *dos iz nit farfallen* (it is not lost), and a special *mo'ed* (appointed time) is made for him, so that after he purifies himself, he may approach the *Beis HaMikdash* and enter within the threshold, etc.

(From a letter, 27 Sivan, 5711)

... Regarding the receipt of two copies of the publication, it is evident from the cover and the changes therein that they obtained a license for its publication, and not necessarily as an internal one, and surely they will write about this soon as well. May it be the will that it be in a good and successful hour, and may the publication succeed in being a channel through which the inwardness of the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs will come—both in their immediate environment and also in an environment that, for the time being, is not yet close. As is known, the saying of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, is that the lesson from *Pesach Sheni* is that one must always rectify, even that which was [due to being] impure or on a distant journey, and even—"for you"—that he did it of his own will.

## 196

And in matters such as these, I am reminded of the saying of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, who said upon his arrival in the United States for the second time, that although the custom of the world is that they do not want competition and *nachmachen* (copying), the approach of Lubavitch in general, and my approach in particular, is: if only the number of those wanting to work in the areas of his work would increase, in his manner and in his way.

It is wondrous that also in this work, as in many points in the activities and matters of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, we see a likeness among the leaders of Israel in our days—that the leader in our days, in the language of the *Tikkunei Zohar*, is an "extension of Moshe." Even Yehoshua, his servant who would not depart from the tent, nevertheless, he proposed to him, as it were, at least as the Sages say, "impose upon them the *tzitzin* (the burden of leadership)," and while he was yet speaking, the faithful shepherd of Israel answered, "Would that all the people of Hashem were prophets, that Hashem would give His spirit upon them." That is to say, even if he does not insist that it be specifically in the manner stated before this by the Holy One, blessed be He—"and I will take of the spirit that is upon you and put it upon them"—but rather, "give His spirit upon them"... And as mentioned above, thank you in advance for your efforts to the best of your ability in allocating help for our work in the aforementioned, and to the greatest extent possible.

(From a letter, 2 Adar, 5716)

... At the end of the book, under the entry *Bas Kol* (Heavenly Voice).

It should be noted regarding the halachic ruling that the *halacha* follows Rav in matters of prohibition and Shmuel in matters of monetary law, because the primary occupation of each of them was—Rav in prohibitions and Shmuel in monetary law, as the Rosh says regarding the aforementioned matter. In such a case, it is understood that the *halacha* follows the Arizal for the reason mentioned, who explained at length the differences in the levels of prophecy, including the matter of the *Bas Kol*.

One should note regarding the *halacha* the matter that "we do not pay attention to a *Bas Kol*," especially since this is marked in every place in the *Talmudic Encyclopedia* edited by the great Rabbi S.Y. Zevin, under the entry *Bas Kol*, and in *Shem HaGedolim* of the Chida, under the entry of our teacher Rabbi Yaakov the Chassid, and in the introduction of Rabbi Reuven Margolies to the book *Responsa Min HaShamayim*...

(From a letter, the year 5722)


## שלח

## 197

### Shelach

I was pleased to read in your letter that you have taken a deep interest in, and have also familiarized yourself with, the situation of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established). This is, after all, one of the consequences of Ahavas Yisrael: "that another person’s situation should truly concern you."

It would be a pity if the information and impressions you have gathered were to be lost. You have likely written them down, or at least the main points. If so, I would be grateful if you could send them to me (with the understanding that they will be returned).

In any event, I would ask you to answer me, if possible, regarding the following questions (which I have listed in the order of the points you raised in your letter):

a) The impression from your visit to Kfar Chabad.
b) The spirit in which the students of the various educational institutions are learning.
c) Data regarding the number of children who are under the influence of the various political parties.
d) Information regarding the spiritual life in the *ma'abarot* (transit camps) in general, and regarding the education there in particular.
e) Surely you have reflected on the Sidra that we just read yesterday morning: (Shelach 14:8-9) "If Hashem desires us, He will bring us... and give it to us" (and when He gives it to us, it will be) "a land flowing with milk and honey" (but there is an eternal condition attached): "Only do not rebel against Hashem." (And when they cried out — ibid., verses 40-42 — "Here we are, and we will go up... but Moshe said... Do not go up" — and do you know why?) "For Hashem is not in your midst."

And this is the main point I am seeking to find out regarding the situation there. Do you have information about this? Not the situation in the land of Canaan, not even [merely] in Eretz Yisrael, but the situation in the *Eretz HaKodesh* (the Holy Land), which will be built and established speedily in our days, literally, by Mashiach Tzidkeinu—if Jews, wherever they may be, whether in the exile here or in the exile

## 198

there, will fulfill what Mashiach said: that he is coming today, "if only you will listen to His voice" (Sanhedrin 98a).

With regards to your family (may they live), and with blessings.
(From a letter dated 27 Sivan, 5711)

... May it be the will [of Hashem] that, finally, you will inform me not only regarding meetings and resolutions about good activities, but also regarding good activities in practice. Especially since it is the subject of the day, according to what is explained in *Likutei Torah* on the Parsha we read this Shabbos: that the ultimate purpose is the deed, and then "the land is very, very good," as opposed to when one wishes to remain in the world of speech. And as I have written many times, it is easy to know, even without contemplation and even for one who is not a man of understanding, that we are not at all utilizing the influence that is given from Above, neither in spiritual matters nor in material matters. Furthermore, there are about two weeks left until 12-13 Tammuz; will there be a *farbrengen*? Who will be responsible, etc.? And as mentioned above, the purpose of speech is that it should lead to action.

With blessings for good tidings, and there is no true good unless the study and the *Midrash* lead to action.
(From a letter dated 27 Sivan, 5718)

I have been informed of a request for a blessing for him and his wife (may they live). They should remember, at a time of favor, the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (of blessed memory). May the merit of these days—the days of Parshas Shelach and its conclusion, the Parsha of *Tzitzis*—since he was particularly careful with it, to influence the many in this matter—stand for him and his wife for long life and good years, and to receive much Chassidishe *nachas* from all their children (may they live). He should look into the book *Kitzurim L'Tanya*, page 46, the saying of the Baal Shem Tov: that even the Angel Michael, the greatest of the angels, would give all his *avodah* and his comprehension in *Elokus* even for just one *mitzvah* of *Tzitzis* out of the four *tzitzis* that every Jew has. See the note there in the aforementioned book, page 150.

With blessings for proper health and good tidings regarding himself, his family, and those he influences (may they live).
(From a letter dated 23 Sivan, 5715)

## 199

... Regarding what you noted concerning the *mitzvah* of *Tzitzis*: whether one fulfills the *mitzvah* every hour that one is dressed in *Tzitzis*, or only at the first moment, similar to the taking of the *Lulav*.

The matter is understood from what is said: "And you shall see it and remember," and just as the remembrance is at every moment of the *mitzvah*, so too is the reason for it—the seeing—the same. This is explicitly stated by the *Rishonim* in *Sefer HaYirah* by Rabbeinu Yonah, near the beginning, where he writes: "The essence of the *mitzvah* of *Tzitzis* is to wear them constantly." (This is the version of the Gra in his commentary to *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, beginning of Siman 24, and such is also the opinion of the Gra; see there). And in *Piskei Dinim* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Orach Chaim* Siman 2, subsection 7, it is implied that it is his opinion that at every hour this is a *mitzvah d'oraisa* (and not merely a *hiddur* of the Rabbis). See also the commentary of the Ibn Ezra on Bamidbar 15:39, where it is also proven to be so.

With blessings for long life and good years.
(From a letter dated 27 Nissan, 5714)

... 5) Inserting the thread into the hole from the side—in *Tallis Gadol*, the Alter Rebbe writes in his *Siddur*: "After he has made the upper knot properly."

6) Regarding what you noted in the above concerning clarifying the length and width—see *Piskei Dinim* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Orach Chaim* Siman 11.
(From a letter during the days of Selichos, 5715)

... It is surely superfluous to point out and urge the necessity of continuing to correspond with his son-in-law, the husband of his daughter mentioned above, Rabbi... to explain to him in detail the magnitude of the merit and the responsibility that rests upon him to bring the hearts of the Children of Israel closer to their Father in Heaven. We do not know how far this reaches; sometimes, by bringing one Jew closer, one establishes generations of sons and daughters who are G-d-fearing and trembling at His word. Consequently, every effort, toil, and labor—toil of the soul and toil of the body—is worthwhile, even for the sake of one Jewish soul, which is not only a "full world" in itself, but also, simply, in terms of his seed and the seed of his seed until the end of all the world (and it is known in *Chassidus* that "the end of all the world"—*sof kol ha'olam*—means that they bring an end to the *helem* and *hester* [the concealment and hiddenness of G-dliness]). May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant us that we see this with physical eyes, literally, for this comes through the *bitachon* (trust) that is above *ta'am v'da'as* (reason and intellect). As is also known, this is one of the meanings of the word *tzitz* and *tzitzis*. *Tzitz* is from the expression, "Behold, he stands behind our wall... peering (*metzitz*) through the lattices" (see *Likutei Torah*, *Sefer Devarim* 91c), which refers to the time of exile. And the place of the *tzitz* was on the forehead—the concept of *bitachon* and connection that is above *ta'am v'da'as*. See...


## קרח

## 200

### Korach

...It appears to me that the status of the Kohanim in relation to the Third Beis Hamikdash is superior to their status in the Mishkan and the first two Temples.

In those instances, the beginning was such that it was impossible to "build the Beis Hamikdash" otherwise, as "everyone is obligated to build and support it with their own bodies and their own money" (Rambam, Hilchos Beis HaBechirah, Chapter 1, Halacha 12).

This is not the case for the Third Beis Hamikdash, which (according to many opinions) is already built and perfected, and will be revealed and descend from Shomayim — see Rashi, Sukkah 41a, end of side a; and further, see the Encyclopedia Talmudit, entry *Beis Hamikdash*, note 60. Even regarding the Rambam (Hilchos Melachim, beginning and end of Chapter 11), one could say that he is describing the certain scenario, even if they were not worthy, in which case Moshiach will build the Beis Hamikdash. There is no disagreement here (as is well known, the rule is not to multiply disputes).

In that future Beis Hamikdash, the Kohanim will begin (with the dedication of the Beis Hamikdash and the Mizbe'ach, as explained in the prophecy of Yechezkel the Kohen), and the Leviim will "join themselves unto thee," etc.

(From a letter dated 3 Menachem Av, 5738)


## חוקת

## 201

### Chukas

...In the parsha we read this past Shabbos, the first verse is "This is the statute (*chukas*) of the Torah." In the teachings of Chassidus, it is explained that the word *chukas* has an additional meaning, related to the term *chakikah* (engraving). This serves as a hint that Jews must study Torah and perform mitzvos in a manner of *chakikah*. This is not like writing with ink, where the ink is one distinct entity and the parchment upon which one writes is another, and they are only subsequently brought together and joined to one another. Rather, the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos must be in a manner of *chakikah*—like carving letters into stone, where the letters are of the very same stone itself, not something added from the outside. So too, in the performance of mitzvos and the study of Torah, it must be a matter of *chakikah*, such that the person, the Torah, and the mitzvos are one thing. And then, the Torah says, "If you walk in My statutes (*chukosai*)"—from the language of *chakikah*—"then I will provide your rains in their time, and the land will yield its produce," etc.

With blessings for a speedy recovery.
(From a letter dated 14 Tammuz, 5714)

...Regarding the difficulty raised in the *kuntres* *Shaar HaSukkos*, in the *maamar* beginning "Lehavin Maamar HaZohar Parshas Emor," where it is written there: "However, metal and stone—their flat objects (*peshutim*) are tamei... and wooden vessels that are flat are tahor..." yet it is explicitly stated in the Gemara (Shabbos 58a) that stone vessels are not susceptible to tumah.

There are several ways to explain this, some of which are forced, and one may choose as they see fit:

1) In that *kuntres*, it brings all the divisions regarding what is susceptible to tumah, including the distinction between flat objects and vessels, and where there is no distinction between flat objects and vessels regarding susceptibility to tumah. Stone falls into the latter category, because in the instance where there is susceptibility to tumah, there is no distinction between a flat object and a vessel, and that is in the tumah of *golel v'dofek* (see Tosafos, s.v. *ad*, Kesuvos 4b).

2) Seemingly, it appears to me that the tumah of *golel v'dofek* is a function of wood (Chullin 129a), which is why one may use for *sechach* materials that are susceptible to the tumah of *golel v'dofek*, such as boards that were fashioned as a cover for a chest. According to this, one could explain that the *kuntres* first clarifies the law of vegetation—that as long as it is growing, it is not susceptible to tumah at all—and afterwards explains two categories within inanimate matter: one where there is a distinction between a vessel and a flat object, and one where there is no distinction between them. For the foundation of this *drush* is the connection between the concepts of vessels and tumah, and the second category consists of metals and stone, for in both of them, the tumah is not dependent on the definition of a "vessel" (in metals, even a flat object is susceptible to tumah; in stone, even a vessel...).


## י"ב תמוז

## 203

### 12-13 Tammuz

In the days of the *Chag HaGeulah*, 12-13 Tammuz, which are approaching, I suggest that we study the *hemshech* of *Chassidus* "Rachav-D" Omer" by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It is printed in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah*, Tammuz 5704 and onwards, and also in *Sefer HaMaamarim Yiddish*, page 165 and onwards.

We are also publishing, in connection with these days of *geulah*, the fourth part of his *reshimah* regarding his final imprisonment. This *reshimah* was written by him during the period of his imprisonment, 15 Sivan 5688, in Riga. The first part was published for 12-13 Tammuz 5712 (*Likkut* 34), the second part for 12-13 Tammuz 5713 (*Likkut* 35), and the third part for 12-13 Tammuz 5714 (*Likkut* 36).

As an addition, at the end of the booklet, there is a *reshimah* of the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he spoke on Sunday, *Parshas Balak* 5687, before his departure to his city of refuge, Kostroma, as recorded by one of the listeners.

* * *

The significance of this celebration has already been explained by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his letter for the first 12-13 Tammuz celebration in the year 5688:

He established it as a day of *farbrengen* and *hisorerus* to strengthen Torah and *Yiddishkeit* in every place, according to its circumstances, and he blessed: "All our brethren who love Torah, study it, and teach it in public—may Hashem grant them life—may Hashem open His good treasury and bestow upon them, and upon all our brethren the Children of Israel—may they live—an abundance of life and great blessing without measure, and may He strengthen their hearts to add courage in disseminating Torah and upholding *Yiddishkeit*, and may we all merit to see children and grandchildren occupied with Torah and *mitzvos* with *harchavah* and good livelihood."

May the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfill the blessings of the *Tzaddik*, the *Nasi* of our generation, in their entirety.

(From a letter, 3 Tammuz 5715)

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the well-known and famous matter of the *Chag HaGeulah* of 12-13 Tammuz, on which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, went out—at that time—to freedom. This was not a private victory, but a victory of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and *Yiddishkeit*, and these days are days of *segulah*.

## 205

It has been a long time since I received any news from you, both regarding your personal affairs and your communal activities. May it be the will of Hashem that this is a sign that everything is in order and in peace.

You are surely aware of our custom that in connection with the days of the *geulah* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—his *geulah* from his imprisonment for his *avodah* with *mesiras nefesh* to uphold Torah and its *mitzvos*—which at the time was an exemplary victory over the forces opposing Hashem and His Torah, and which also serves as a clear lesson for the years and generations that followed, that Torah rules over reality even if one finds no place for this in human intellect:

We publish specifically for these days a book or booklet on the *inyana d'yoma*, containing matters of *hisorerus* regarding this.

Enclosed here is the booklet published this year, a part of the *reshimos* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding his imprisonment. As an addition, there are the words of the *Nasi* of Israel, based on the point that in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, every single Jew is a free man, and has no one but Hashem, his G-d.

And if one needs a reminder and *hisorerus* in this—regarding exile among non-Jews and their decrees, where they have no choice and are merely like an axe in the hand of the one who hews with it—then all the more so is this *hisorerus* necessary regarding exile among Jews, who have free choice, as it is written: "See, I have set before you today life and the good... and you shall choose life." And although the request of the *Ribono shel Olam* (which is also help and assistance) is "and you shall choose life," just as the matter of "life" is emphasized, so too is it emphasized that it must be "and you shall choose."

With blessings for good tidings,

(From a letter, 18 Tammuz 5715)

I have received your participation in our *chinuch* work in North Africa, and the receipt is enclosed.

I hope to hear good news from you and your family—may they live—always.

With blessings for success,

On this bright day of *Chag HaGeulah*, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, is surely offering *rinah* and *tefillah* for his *mekusharim* in particular, and for all those who act for Torah and the *maor shebaTorah* with *mesiras nefesh*, that the *Ribono shel Olam* should make their participation easier and enable them to increase their participation, with proper health and with *harchavah* in *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

It is known that one of the reasons why a *taanis chalom* (fast for a dream) is permitted on *Shabbos* is that since it is a time of *taanug*, it is impossible to suffer pain in the world, and consequently, all *dinim* are nullified through this.

And since today is a day of joy, the day of the joy, *geulah*, and redemption of the soul of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who, as he writes in his letter, "The *Ribono shel Olam* did not redeem me alone on 12 Tammuz, but also all those who love our holy Torah, who keep the *mitzvos*, and also those who are called by the name of Israel," therefore

## 207

on this day of joy, all matters of *dinim* and *mochin d'katnus*, etc., will surely be nullified, and there will be no more sorrow.

With blessings of comfort,

May it be the will of the *Ribono shel Olam* that it be successful, and may the *Ribono shel Olam* expand their borders with students, both in quality and in quantity—that is, in increasing the number of students and raising their quality, fitting for the name of the *Yeshiva*, *Achai Temimim*.

(From a letter, 19 Tammuz 5726)

...I was happy to hear from [name] and also to see from the press that you are continuing your publications, at least from time to time. This strengthens my hope that you are still active in the primary task of every Jew, as the *Mishnah* says: "I was created to serve my Maker"—by disseminating the Torah of His Maker, that is the *Ribono shel Olam*, and encouraging the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* of His Maker wherever your hand can reach.

## 213

The power of influence. And surely here too it is unnecessary to elaborate that the intent of *yirah* comes first—in its simple sense, for then the study leads to practical *mitzvos*. As the wisest of all men summarized, after all the searching and inquiry: "Fear G-d (the *yirah* that leads to) and keep His *mitzvos*, for this is the whole man."

The month of Tammuz is marked for us by the days of *segulah* of 12-13 of the month, the days of the *geulah* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, from his imprisonment in the Soviet Union. The chronicles of the leaders of Israel must serve as a living moral lesson and study, and the inner point of the aforementioned days of *geulah* is that one who truly fights for the truth, to the point of actual *mesiras nefesh*, and especially in a matter that concerns the many, even one person can stand before and against a mighty regime and even overcome it.

With respect and blessing,

(From a letter, end of Tammuz 5719)

I received with pleasure your letter from the day of the *hillula* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the *pardes* of Torah concerning the name of the *baal hillula*. For if it is said about every person that the *Ribono shel Olam* places in the mouths of the parents that name which is necessary for that soul according to its place in the *Adam HaElyon* from which it was hewn, and this name is inscribed above on the *Kisei HaKavod* (see *Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 23; see also *Emek HaMelech*, Gate 1, end of Chapter 4; *Ohr HaChaim HaKadosh*, Devarim 29:19; *Degel Machaneh Ephraim* on *Bereishis*, and more), then all the more so is this true of the name of the *Nasi* of Israel, whose soul is the aspect of the "head and brain" for the souls of our generation, as brought in the holy *Tanya*, Chapter 2.

One should add a hint to the verse in your letter, based on what is explained, that *Yosef* is in *gematria* six times *Havayah* (*Likkutei Torah* of the *AriZal*, *Parshas Vayeishev*, and elsewhere), and he was the sixth generation from our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, founder of the *Chabad Chassidus*. And *Yitzchak* is in *gematria* eight times *Havayah* (*Pri Etz Chaim*, commentary on *Haggadah*, and elsewhere), for he was the eighth generation from the *Baal Shem Tov*, founder of the general *Chassidus* (see also *Likkutei Torah* of the *AriZal*, end of *Parshas Vayeira*, regarding the connection between *Yosef* and *Yitzchak* and the aforementioned *gematria*). And as is known in the interpretation of our Sages on the verse "In the beginning G-d created," the *Ribono shel Olam* wanted to create the world with the attribute of *din*; He saw that the world could not endure, so He associated with it the attribute of *rachamim*, as it is written, "On the day that Hashem G-d made earth and heaven." The interpretation of this association is miraculous conduct in the world through the *Tzaddikim*, and all this is hinted at in the names themselves: *Yosef*—"to say, 'Hashem will add another son for me,'" and the *Admur HaTzemach Tzedek* explained that he transforms the "other" into a "son." *Yitzchak*—"G-d has made laughter for me," through the clarification and refinement of the concealment of the name *Elokim*, which is a shield for the name *Havayah*, "our mouth will be filled with laughter" in the future to come (see *Midrash HaNe'elam*, *Bereishis* 115a and onwards), through the *avodah* of clarification and refinement in this time of exile. And one who contemplates

## 214

the life story of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in this world and his actions, will see that the two who are one, as mentioned above, are the foundation and purpose of his *avodah* in holiness.

(From a letter, 21 Shevat 5715)

To each and every resident of *Kfar Chabad* and to all participants in the *farbrengen*.

May it be His will that the *Kfar*, its residents, and its affairs, both internally and externally, be redeemed from all obstacles and delays to their development and expansion in quantity and quality. In particular, may the *Beis HaKnesses* and *Beis HaMedrash* fulfill its role to elevate all matters in *gashmius* and *ruchnius* up the ladder of *tefillah*, and to draw down all blessings below via the ladder of the revealed Torah and *Chassidus*. And with *harchavah* in all things, may they spread the *maayanos* in their surroundings and throughout the Holy Land, until our true and complete *geulah* through *Mashiach Tzidkeinu* very soon. A *Chassidishe* and successful *farbrengen*.

(Telegram, 10 Tammuz 5719)

## 215

*Farbrengens* of the days of *geulah* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, and our own *geulah*—may they be joyful and active. Especially with the speed of erecting all the buildings and completing them soon—buildings in the simple sense and spiritual buildings, which will walk together, as per the instruction of the *Baal Shem Tov* that "you shall surely help with him" (*azov ta'azov imo*). And with *harchavah*, may they spread his *maayanos* outward, and may Hashem soon establish the border of the widow with the coming of *Malka Meshicha*.

(Telegram, 11 Tammuz 5720)

Active *farbrengens*, and may they be continued throughout the entire year, with the blessing of *Chag HaGeulah*.

(Telegram for 12-13 Tammuz 5726)
