## פינחס

## 223

### Pinchas

It was well written that there is a distinction between *goral* (lot) and *yerushah* (inheritance). As explained in the *maamar* "Ashreinu" (2 Nissan 5700), the portions of *goral* and *yerushah* are: the *avodah* of the heart, the mind, and the *hargashas Elokus* (feeling of Divinity) in every matter, which is present in *yerushah*. This is the *avodah* of *nefesh, ru'ach, neshamah*, of *ratzon* (will) and *taanug* (pleasure), the point of Yiddishkeit, the specific *chiyus* (vitality), the general *chiyus*, and the *chai b'etzem* (life in essence). It is the specific *avodah* of the *nefesh habehamis* and *nefesh elokis*, the general *avodah*, and the *avodah* of the *nefesh elokis* from its own essence (see the *maamar* "B'Chodesh HaShevi'i" 5692).

However, the suggestion that *yerushah* is more similar to *goral* than to other forms of acquisition—both in *nigleh* (the revealed Torah) and in *nistar* (the hidden Torah)—is, in my humble opinion, incorrect. On the contrary: in *nigleh*, *yerushah* is superior to other forms of acquisition in that it is an inevitable acquisition, whereas *goral* is less significant than other forms of acquisition, to the point that some say it is not an acquisition at all (see the commentaries on *Gemara Bava Basra* 106b; *Shulchan Aruch Choshen Mishpat* 273 and sources cited there). This also aligns with the *nistar*, because the *hargashas Elokus*, the point of Yiddishkeit, etc., exists within everyone, and even at the time of sin, "it was faithful with him" (*Tanya*, *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, ch. 24). Following this comes the specific *avodah* of *Torah* and *mitzvos* that everyone is obligated in. Above that is the general *avodah*, etc. (or the preference and extra caution, which is also among the distinctions between a portion and a *goral*; see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, end of ch. 7).

(It seems that what caused some confusion is that in the *nistar*, the revelation mentioned above that comes through *yerushah* comes about through the prior *avodah* of the portion and the *goral*. One could say that a parallel to this exists in the division of the Land, where the *yerushah* is theirs from their forefathers—*Bava Basra* 119b—but it was only revealed in practice after they conquered it—the specific war: "The king of Jericho, one," etc.—and divided it by *goral*. See *Tosafos*, s.v. *V'lo*, *Rosh Hashanah* 13a; *Yerushalmi, Challah*, beginning of ch. 2; *Parashas Derachim*, *Drush* 9, and elsewhere. But this is not the place to elaborate.)

(From a letter dated 27 Nissan 5706)


## מטות-­מסעי

## 223

### Matos-Masei

Both parshios emphasize the entry into Eretz Yisrael in the true and complete Geulah, and the instruction that everyone must prepare themselves for the entry into Eretz Yisrael by redeeming themselves from the matters of the world, as is the content of the ruling of the Rambam (at the end of Hilchos Shmittah V'Yovel).

## 224

1. We are currently on the fourth day of Parshas Matos-Masei. In such a calendar arrangement, the fourth day openly and simply connects the two parshios, for in the Chumash lesson for the fourth day, one studies the conclusion of Parshas Matos and the beginning of Parshas Masei in one continuous sequence. From this, it is understood that the content of the end of Parshas Matos and the beginning of Parshas Masei are related to one another.

The explanation of this matter:
Both speak of the entry into Eretz Yisrael. The end of Parshas Matos speaks of the conquest and settlement of the Transjordan (which is like the beginning of the entry into Eretz Yisrael), and Parshas Masei speaks of the forty-two journeys in the desert, until the final journey: "And they traveled... and camped in the plains of Moav by the Jordan of Jericho", in proximity to Jericho, which was the "lock of Eretz Yisrael".

On a deeper level, both emphasize and hint at the matter of the entry into Eretz Yisrael that will take place in the true and complete Geulah:
It was explained previously that the request of the tribes of Gad and Reuven to receive their inheritance across the Jordan (as recounted at length at the end of Parshas Matos) was for the good, because they wanted to merit the beginning of the inheritance of the land of the ten nations (which will be in its completeness in the future) immediately upon entering the land, by receiving at that time the land of Sichon and Og, which also included part of the land of Amon and Moav (which is part of the land of the Keini, Knizi, and Kadmoni).

Similarly, in the continuation of the Chumash lesson—at the beginning of Parshas Masei—it says, "These are the journeys of the Bnei Yisrael who went out from the land of Egypt according to their legions..." It is explained in Likutei Torah that even though this verse speaks of the journey "who went out from the land of Egypt"—meaning a single journey—it is nevertheless written "These are the journeys" (in the plural), because the purpose of all forty-two journeys is to go out from *Mitzrayim* (Egypt), which comes from the word *meitzarim* (limitations/boundaries). Therefore, they are all called "who went out from the land of Egypt," because the departure from all limitations and boundaries is completed only with their encampment at the Jordan of Jericho, which hints at the Geulah through Moshiach (*d'morach v'dain*).

From this, it is also understood conversely that the departure from Egypt included all forty-two journeys, because from the departure from Egypt, they were supposed to enter Eretz Yisrael immediately (as it is in its completeness—the land of the ten nations, including the land of the Keini, Knizi, and Kadmoni, which is across the Jordan to the east).

## 225

2. "The Torah is eternal", and from this, it is understood that this reading contains an eternal instruction for every time and every place.

The instruction is, simply put, that Bnei Yisrael must be prepared to enter Eretz Yisrael (as it is in its completeness, the land of the ten nations). And not only prepared to enter the land, but they must actually enter the land [for as long as they have not entered the land in actuality, even while standing "by the Jordan of Jericho" in proximity to Eretz Yisrael, they are still in Galus (and even in the Galus of Egypt, as mentioned above, that even this final journey is called "who went out from the land of Egypt")].

And all the more so in our time now, as we stand in the final days of Galus, prepared to enter immediately into the true and complete Geulah—we must finish all matters of Galus today, at the end of Parshas Matos, before the beginning of Parshas Masei (in such a way that in Parshas Masei we enter Eretz Yisrael in actuality, and even to the Eretz Yisrael in its completeness, the land of the ten nations).

This is done by each and every person redeeming themselves through the addition of all matters of Torah and Mitzvos in general. As explained in Tanya, every matter of Torah and Mitzvos is a "private Geulah," and since "the name Geulah has ascended", it is also the beginning of the general Geulah —the redemption of each and every one of Yisrael, within the collective of Yisrael, in all corners of the world.

It can be said that this is the content of the Rambam's ruling : "Not only the tribe of Levi, but every single person... whose spirit moves him... he is sanctified as holy of holies, and Hashem will be his portion and his inheritance forever and ever... for David, peace be upon him, says, 'Hashem is the portion of my inheritance and my cup; You support my lot'"—that every one of Yisrael can redeem themselves from the matters of the world and be sanctified as holy of holies, the title and level of a Kohen Gadol.

Furthermore: The Rambam rules that "the lighting of the candles is valid when performed by non-Kohanim," for it is within the power of a non-Kohen to light the "pure olive oil" in the "menorah of pure gold" that is in the Beis Hamikdash [and to the extent that for this reason, the Menorah is brought outside —which, relative to the Sanctuary, is akin to a state of Galus].

This means that it is in the power of every one of Yisrael (even a non-Kohen) to light the Menorah, not only in spiritual matters—in the "menorah of pure gold" that is within each one of Yisrael, by making oneself "pure olive oil," which indicates the ultimate level of refinement and purification—but also in the Beis Hamikdash literally.

[This can be connected to the days of the month in which we currently stand—as we enter the 26th day of the month, the gematria of the name *Havayah* ("Hashem is his inheritance"), and afterwards, the 27th day of the month, which hints at "pure olive oil."]

3. And so it shall be for us in these very moments,

## 226

And until this very moment (in the singular) literally—that through every man and woman performing their service in a manner of "his spirit moves him," out of generosity of heart —with a healthy heart and a healthy soul (soul within a body), and "the heart divides to all the limbs", we immediately finish all matters of Galus. And immediately thereafter—the beginning of the complete Geulah, which is also a true Geulah, a Geulah after which there is no Galus.

And we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And you shall be gathered one by one, Bnei Yisrael." And since this comes through the Holy One, Blessed be He, Himself, it can happen in one moment literally, and simply put—one moment on the clock (no more than one second, "a moment like the blink of an eye").

"Coming with the clouds of heaven", immediately in the moment thereafter, all Bnei Yisrael are found—from all four corners of the earth, our young and our old, our sons and our daughters —in the Holy Land, and in Jerusalem the Holy City (which is the "capital city" of all Eretz Yisrael, including the land of the Keini, Knizi, and Kadmoni, which is across the Jordan to the east), in the Beis Hamikdash, and in the Holy of Holies [where the first Tablets are found with the final Tablets, and through this, we also transform the middle forty days (in which we are now) into days of favor].

To the point that the entire world becomes a "dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed (in the lower realms)", akin to a person's dwelling literally, where a person is found in all their matters, both in physicality (their body and even their garments) and in spirituality (their soul and spirit, with all their will, down to the inwardness of their will and pleasure)—similarly, the entire world becomes a "dwelling place for Him," where in this lowest world and in the physicality of the world, the true and inward will of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is revealed.

4. And all these matters—simply and literally, to the point that "he points with his finger and says, 'This'" (akin to "These are the journeys," "These are the words"), and Moshe and Aharon are with them, including "Pinchas the son of Elazar the son of Aharon the Kohen," who was also a "anointed for war", through whom comes the victory in the wars of Hashem, including the war of the house of David, David the King Moshiach, as per the ruling of the Rambam that when he fights the war of Hashem and is victorious, he is certainly Moshiach.

[And this is connected to the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And the kingdom shall be Hashem's" in all corners of the world, and all the more so in the Holy Land, which is called "Eretz Yisrael"—named for "For you have struggled with G-d and with men and have prevailed," the matter of dominion and kingship].

And furthermore, and most importantly—immediately and instantly, and with alacrity.

## 227

Especially since, as is customary, we conclude by giving a mission (mitzvah) of *tzedakah* to each and every one within the collective of Yisrael, and we give something that has substance.

[For according to Torah, a *prutah* has substance, to the extent that a woman is betrothed "with a *prutah* or the value of a *prutah*". And it should be noted that this is one of the innovations of the true and complete Geulah, for then the marriage of the Holy One, Blessed be He, and Bnei Yisrael will be in ultimate perfection, and afterwards all the seven blessings, together with "A new Torah shall go forth from Me", including all matters of innovation, down to the innovation of the tenth—"The tenth shall be holy"].

For *tzedakah* is great, as it brings the Geulah closer and hastens the Geulah. And not only "brings closer," but immediately and instantly the true and complete Geulah comes through David the King Moshiach (together with "Pinchas, this is Eliyahu", the herald of the Geulah), with joy and a good heart, and immediately and instantly.


## קיץ

## 228

### Summer

May it be the will of Hashem that, as per the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, you should have a healthy and happy summer.

Based on the words of our Sages in *Sotah* 10a, Samson was named after Hashem, as it is written, "For Hashem is a sun and shield" (*Tehillim* 84:12)—which is also the allusion to the fact that in the future, Hashem will take the sun out of its sheath. The sun in its full strength in the physical realm is during the summer months; this is an indication that it is the same in the spiritual realm, for physical things are an extension of their spiritual sources. Therefore, it is explained in Chassidus that the *avodah* of Hashem during the summer months is easier than in the winter months.

May you have a healthy and happy summer, both physically and spiritually, and may you be privileged to see your children and their families, may they live, and your son-in-law and his family, may they live, in peace.

With blessings for long life and good years with all the interpretations.

(From a letter dated 10 Tammuz 5713)

***

With the approach of the time when children finish their studies in school, and in connection with this, a change in the household routine and conduct also follows, I hope that the work program of Agudas N'shei U'bnos Chabad is being prepared in good time, adapted to the aforementioned changes—both for those who are already connected and active in the work, and for those Jewish women and girls who are not yet aware of it, or are not aware to a sufficient degree.

## 229

It is clearly evident that work done according to a pre-prepared program has greater success, both in the scope and in the depth of the work.

Coming from Rosh Chodesh Tammuz and finding ourselves a few days before the *Chag HaGeulah*—the liberation festival—of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi* of our generation, on 12-13 Tammuz, this will surely add warmth and dedication to the work. This will further increase the success, as well as Hashem’s blessings in the personal matters of the members and their families, may they live.

May Hashem help that it should be according to the instruction of the well-known teaching of our master, the Baal Shem Tov, on the verse, "When you see the donkey" (*Devarim* 22:4)—meaning, to look closely at the characteristics of the *chamor* (donkey), which relates to *chomer* (matter/the body), and to come to the conclusion that "you shall surely help him" (*azov ta'azov imo*)—to serve Hashem with the body and its affairs together.

And as explained at length in many places in the teachings of Chabad Chassidus, from our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe until my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi* of our generation, this must be done *b'simcha u'v'tuv levav*—with joy and a good spirit.

With wishes for success in all of the above, and in anticipation of good tidings regarding this, and with blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*.

***

To the children of Israel in "Gan Yisrael," and foremost to the counselors, the administration, and all those involved, may they live.

May your arrival at Gan Yisrael be in a good and auspicious hour, and may you continue the success and blessing in all matters of Gan Yisrael, both physical and spiritual. May Gan Yisrael live up to its name by raising good trees that bear good fruit, and may the verse be fulfilled in them: "My beloved (this is Hashem) has come to His garden"—a dwelling place for Him, through the study and fulfillment of our Torah and *mitzvos*, illuminated by the light and vitality of Chassidus.

And the beginning of "Gan Yisrael" this year on the bright day, the day of the redemption of our *Nasi*, the head of Israel,

## 230

and "the body follows the head"—will bring into all matters of "Gan Yisrael" a redemption from all undesirable things, and may it succeed with outstanding success.

With blessings for a good Shabbos.

***

May the opening of "Gan Yisrael" and your entire stay there be with success in everything.

Especially this year, the year of *Shemitah*, which is a Shabbos to Hashem and is auspicious for an increase in Torah and *mitzvos*, and for the drawing down of *shuvah* and *nachas*, the true *taanug*—in matters of both body and soul together, and to hasten the fulfillment of the prophecy in our *parsha*, "A star shall step forth from Jacob," this is King Moshiach, "and Israel shall act valiantly."

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*.

***

## 231

May the opening of "Gan Yisrael" and your entire stay there be with great success.

And as we stand in the year 5750, which, as has been publicized and spread throughout the Jewish diaspora, contains the allusion: "It shall be a year of miracles"—in which Hashem gives every single Jewish man and woman the strength to act in all matters of Judaism, Torah, and *mitzvos* in a manner of miraculous conduct—above their own limitations.

May each of you add, with great joy, to your own education and the education of your surroundings in Torah (which is the heritage of the congregation of Jacob) and its *mitzvos*.

May you continue in this throughout the entire year, and with increase. And all of this will hasten and expedite the fulfillment of the prayer: "I have found David My servant; with My holy oil have I anointed him," in the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for success in all the above, and with blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*.

***

## 232

May the opening of "Gan Yisrael" and your entire stay there be with great success.

May you continue this success in all matters of "Gan Yisrael," both physical and spiritual. May "Gan Yisrael" live up to its name—to sprout good trees that bear good fruit, through the study of our Torah and the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah," which is the inner dimension of the Torah, as is the desire and hope of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the master of the redemption. And Hashem is the Helper.

May you continue in this throughout the entire year, and with increase. And with even greater strength in the year 5751—"It shall be a year of wonders, I will show him."

## 233

Through this, there will be fulfilled in each and every one of them, and within the entire Jewish people, the prayer and blessing of Moshe Rabbeinu at the conclusion and seal of the Psalm of the *Tzaddik* in *Tehillim*: "May the pleasantness of Hashem our G-d be upon us, and the work of our hands establish for us"—may it be His will that the *Shechinah* rests upon the work of your hands—"and the work of our hands, establish it"—in the Third *Beis Hamikdash*, which will be built speedily in our days, in the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, immediately, truly, and now.

With blessings for a good Shabbos and for success in all the above.

## מבצעים, י' המבצעים

## Mivtzoim, The Ten Mivtzoim

[216] The fundamental point of the Mivtzoim is that every single Yid is a shaliach of Hashem, and therefore, every Yid has the capacity—and the responsibility—to influence another Yid. This is not reserved for those who are specifically designated as shluchim, but is a duty incumbent upon every member of anash. Through the performance of a mitzvah, even one that is seemingly minor, a Yid connects himself and the other person to the Ribono shel Olam, thereby bringing about a revelation of Ohr Ein Sof within the world. This is the essence of the avodah of our generation: to transform the world into a dwelling place for Hashem, through the dissemination of Torah and Yiddishkeit to every corner, regardless of the current spiritual state of the individual. By engaging in this, one achieves a state of true bitul, as he recognizes that his own existence is merely a vessel for the will of the Rebbe, and through this hiskashrus, he becomes a conduit for the light of the Geulah.

## עקבתא דמשיחא

## The Footsteps of Moshiach

[157](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/2/157.aspx). The concept of *Ikvesa D’Meshicha*—the "footsteps of Moshiach"—is that the final period before the coming of Moshiach is compared to the heel of the foot. Just as the heel is the lowest part of the body, lacking the vitality and sensitivity of the head or the heart, so too is this generation the lowest level in the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. Yet, precisely because it is the heel, it possesses a unique quality: it is the point of contact with the ground, the very place where the transition to the ultimate revelation occurs. It is specifically through our *avodah* in these "lowest" times—the *iskafya* and *is'hapcha* of the darkness—that we draw down the *Ohr Ein Sof* into the world, transforming the heel itself into a vessel for the revelation of the *Yechidah* of the world. This is the inner meaning of "the footsteps of Moshiach": that the very lowest point of the *galus* is the threshold of the most sublime *geulah*.

## פנימיות התורה

## Pnimiyus HaTorah

[138] The teachings of Chassidus add confidence and joy to the avodah of Hashem. [145] At the giving of the Torah, the revealed Torah was in a state of concealment, while Pnimiyus HaTorah was in a state of revelation. [155] Chassidus is the heritage of all Klal Yisrael and is relevant to every individual. [162] The innovation of the teachings of Chassidus lies in the bitul of "there is nothing else." [190] In our times, the kochos have been granted to anash through the abundance of maamarim that are accessible and sichos that provide explanation and understanding. [232] The light of the Torah.

## קם לי' בדרבה מיני'

## He is liable for the greater penalty (Kam Lei B'diraba Minei)

[131] The principle of *Kam Lei B'diraba Minei*—that one is not punished for a lesser offense when a more severe penalty is incurred through the same act—is rooted in the concept of *bitul*. When a person commits an act that carries multiple levels of liability, the greater penalty effectively nullifies the lesser one, as the essence of the transgression is subsumed within the more severe consequence. This is not merely a legal technicality, but a reflection of how the *dinim* (judgments) are structured within the *Seder Hishtalshelus*. Just as in the realm of *Elokus*, where the lower levels are entirely nullified within the higher levels—as the *Ohr Ein Sof* permeates and transcends all—so too, the severity of the greater punishment encompasses the entirety of the act, leaving no room for the lesser penalty to exist as a separate entity. This is why the Gemara concludes that the lesser liability is "swallowed up" by the greater one; it is an expression of the fundamental *bitul* that exists when a higher, more encompassing reality takes hold.

21:25 In Cheshbon and all its daughters (And Rashi: The villages adjacent to it): [118](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/118.aspx).
21:26 In Rashi: Because it is said, "Do not harass [Moav]," etc.: [87](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/1/87.aspx).
In Rashi: Sichon took it (Ammon and Moav) from them, and through [this] it was purified for Israel: [87](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/1/87.aspx). [224](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/12/224.aspx).
21:27 In Rashi: Bilaam, of whom it is said, "And he took up his parable": [90](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/2/90.aspx).
21:28 From Cheshbon... from the city of Sichon: [117](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/117.aspx).
21:33 And Og, king of Bashan, came out, etc., for battle: [81](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/2/81.aspx).

## מטות

## מטות

[124](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/11/1/124.aspx) (The connection between the parshiyos of Matos-Masei and Devarim to the Bein HaMetzarim period). [224](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/12/224.aspx) (The connection between the parshiyos of Matos and Masei).

30:3 He shall not profane his word: [27](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/27.aspx).

31:2 In Rashi: That they were despoiling them, for it was only said, "Do not provoke them to war": [87](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/1/87.aspx).

32:3 In Rabbeinu Bachya: They were serving avodah zarah, etc., and therefore the Bnei Gad and Bnei Reuven changed the names of the cities to other names, etc.: [120](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/120.aspx).

32:5 Let this land be given to your servants, etc.: [120](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/120.aspx).

32:33-42 [Regarding the conquest and settlement of the Transjordan]: [224](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/12/224.aspx).

32:38 And they changed the names, etc., and they called by names, etc. (And Rashi: The Amorites used to call their cities after the names of their avodah zarah, etc.): [119](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/119.aspx).

In Ramban: And it is the custom of Scripture always, regarding captured cities, to mention the new name: [118](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/118.aspx).

32:41 And Yair the son of Menashe went and captured their villages, etc. (And Rashi: Their villages): [117](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/117.aspx).

And he called them Chavos Yair (And Rashi: Because he had no children, he called them by his name as a memorial): [118](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/118.aspx).

32:42 And he captured Kenas and its daughter-cities: [118](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/118.aspx).

And he called it Novach by his name (And Rashi: The *hei* in *lah* does not have a *mapik*, etc.): [119](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/119.aspx).

In Rashi: That this name did not endure for it: [119](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/119.aspx).

In Megaleh Amukos: The roshei teivos of the name Novach — *Nogah Barak Chanisecha* (The radiance of the lightning of Your spear): [120](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/120.aspx).

34:7: And this shall be for you the northern border (and Rashi: The northern border): [122](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/11/1/122.aspx).

35:26: Who shall flee there: [127](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/11/2/127.aspx).

## שבועות

## Shavuos

13, a. "For he has despised the word of Hashem" — this refers to one who casts off the yoke and interprets the Torah in a brazen manner.

Rashi, s.v. *megaleh panim*: He approaches words of Torah with chutzpah and with an open display of insolence. 

Ibid.: For example, Menashe, who would sit and expound upon the Aggadah in a disparaging manner.

## זבחים

## Zevachim

73a, Tosafos s.v. *v’hatachtonos*: The black ones are not fit, etc. The black ones are noticeable, etc. [61](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/1/61.aspx).
117a-b, Naziriteship offerings are brought on a *bamah*, according to Rabbi Meir . . . They are voluntary offerings (vows and donations). [26](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/26.aspx).
117b, If it was stated, it was stated thus, etc. [26](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/26.aspx).
Rashi s.v. *menachos v’nezirus*: For even though . . . it is an obligation upon him, nevertheless, they came upon him through a vow. [26](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/26.aspx).
Ibid. s.v. *nezirus chovah*: He did not volunteer . . . he became obligated in the offerings of his own accord. [27](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/27.aspx).

## ספרי

###### Naso

6:3 "There is no *nezirah* anywhere except for *perishah* (abstinence)." [31](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/31.aspx).
6:11 "For having sinned..." He requires atonement for having afflicted his soul by abstaining from wine. [31](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/31.aspx).

###### Behaaloscha

10:33 "The way of the *atarim*..." It does not say *taryim* (spies), but rather... (according to the version of Rabbeinu Hillel and others). [78](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/2/78.aspx).
The way of the *atarim*... Aharon died... their great scout (*tayyar*). [78](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/2/78.aspx).

###### Shelach

15:22 "And if you err..." Regarding *avodah zarah*... Just as the one who transgresses [in other matters]... so too regarding *avodah zarah*, he casts off the yoke, breaks the covenant, and interprets the Torah in a distorted manner (*megaleh panim baTorah*). [53](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/53.aspx). [55](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/55.aspx).
According to the commentary of Rabbeinu Hillel: *Megaleh panim baTorah* means that he brazenly defies the Torah by not fulfilling its precepts. [54](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/54.aspx).
In *Sifrei d'bei Rav*: [55](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/55.aspx).
15:23 "All that Hashem has commanded..." Even... as it is said, "from the day..." Anyone who acknowledges *avodah zarah*... [53](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/53.aspx).
15:30 *Megaleh panim baTorah* like Menashe... who would expound upon the *Aggadah* with slanderous intent... [54](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/54.aspx). [55](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/55.aspx).
15:31 "Because he has despised the word of Hashem"—this is one who *megaleh panim baTorah*. [54](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/54.aspx). [55](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/55.aspx).

###### Korach

18:20 "Everything" includes *kohanim*, *levi'im*, and *yisraelim*... "You shall have no inheritance in their land"—this excludes... [103](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/9/1/103.aspx).
18:23 "And in the midst of the Bnei Yisrael they shall have no inheritance..." I might infer... [103](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/9/1/103.aspx).
18:24 "The tithe of the Bnei Yisrael..." The *Makom* (Hashem) called it *terumah* until... (and in the commentaries). [68](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/2/68.aspx).
Because it is said, "And *venashal*..." But we have not heard of the *Keni*, *Kenizi*, and *Kadmoni*; the verse teaches, "Therefore..." [107](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/9/1/107.aspx).
18:29 "Its sanctified portion from it"—this implies that if [the non-sanctified] fell into it, it becomes sanctified; from here they said... [60](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/1/60.aspx). [62](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/1/62.aspx).
18:32 "If you set it apart not from the choicest..." [65](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/2/65.aspx).
"And you shall not profane the holy things..." This is a warning to the *kohanim*... [65](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/2/65.aspx).

###### Chukas

19:15 "And every vessel..." The verse speaks of an earthenware vessel... *Rema*... a vessel that receives *tumah* through its opening... [72](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/1/72.aspx).
A barrel that he turned over on its opening... is *tamei*... [75](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/1/75.aspx).
Vessels of dung... from where do we know [they are susceptible to *tumah*] regarding earth? It is a logical deduction... [72](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/1/72.aspx).

###### Pinchas

26:53 "Everything" includes *yisraelim*, *kohanim*, and *levi'im* (there is a version regarding the order)... *kohanim* are excluded... [103](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/9/1/103.aspx).

###### Re'eh

11:28 "From the way..." From here they said: Anyone who acknowledges *avodah zarah* is as one who denies the entire Torah... [56](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/2/56.aspx).

## קהלת רבה

## Koheles Rabbah

"Seven complete weeks shall they be" (Vayikra 23:15) — when are they "complete"? At a time when there is no *Yeshu* (ego) and *Shechinas* (the Divine Presence) among them (and so it is brought in the name of the *Rokeach*). [8]


## תנחומא

## Tanchuma

### Tisa
21 And I descend at Sinai with My tetramorphs [146].

### Behaaloscha
3 Moshe was perplexed... "Take gold"... He would strike with a hammer and it would form itself [33]. [34].
"So Moshe did"—it does not say here [that Moshe did it], rather, who did it? Hashem [33]. [37].

6 The face of Moshe turned pale, etc. [98].

Amalek was always a strap of chastisement for Yisrael, etc. [81].

2 "And Moav was afraid"... Yisrael appeared to the Moavites as armed... whatever you can seize, etc. [87].

## יד החזקה

## יד החזקה

[19](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/19.aspx) (The headings for the laws are the language of the Rambam). [30](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/2/30.aspx) (His approach is to copy the laws of the Gemara verbatim). [107](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/9/1/107.aspx) (It is not his way to write novel concepts, etc.).
Introduction: The Babylonian Gemara . . after . . the Jerusalem Gemara by approximately one hundred years: [45](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/2/45.aspx).
The 248 positive mitzvos correspond to the number of a person’s limbs: [22](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/22.aspx).

## דרוש וחידוש (רעק"א)

## Drush V’Chiddush (R’ Akiva Eiger)

**Kesuvos**
33b, s.v. Yacholni: The reason that if a murderer leaves his city of refuge, anyone is not liable for him [for killing him]. 

**Chinuch**
Mitzvah 284: "And you shall not profane the holy things of the Bnei Yisrael, etc." — this is a prohibition against eating *maaser rishon* while it is *tevel*. 
Mitzvah 306: "And there are those who say, etc." — all of them are one mitzvah, etc. 
Because the entire essence of Yisrael is nothing but the Torah, etc., we were commanded to count from the morrow, etc., and his entire desire is to reach that time. 
The mitzvah of counting for a *zavah* is nothing but an observation of the days, etc., and not that they are obligated to count them verbally.

## קהלת יעקב

## The Appearance of a Flaring Fire, the Appearance of a Great Cloud, and the Appearance of a Stormy Wind

**The appearance of a flaring fire, the appearance of a great cloud, and the appearance of a stormy wind**
[Fire, cloud, and wind are the Binah and ZON of the kelipah]:.

**The appearance of the four kelipos**
The three kelipos are the Chesed, Gevurah, Tiferes, Netzach, Hod, Yesod, and Malchus of the kelipah, while the Keter, Chochma, and Binah are [from the side of] the Ein Sof, and so on:.


## הקריאה והקדושה

## The Calling and the Holiness

## ראבי"ה

## Pesachim

Sotah 126 [Explanation of the Midrash: "When are they 'complete'? When there is salvation and the Shechinah among them"]:.
The version in the Midrash is: "When are they 'complete'? When there is the salvation of the Shechinah among them":.


## ראב"ן

## Ra'avan

The end of the entry [explaining the Midrash: "When are they 'complete'? When Yeshua and Shechinah are among them"]:.

The version in the Midrash is: "When are they 'complete'? When the Yeshua of the Shechinah is among them":.

## מפתח ספרי חסידות

## From our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im


## כתר שם טוב

## Kesser Shem Tov

Sefer Mitzvos Gadol: According to a person’s thoughts... so do they pass before him in the physical, etc..

Sefer Tziyoni: Thought... can nullify it..

Sefer Reishis Chochma: When... one can grasp the thought of his fellow in the manner that he desires, etc..


## תניא

## Tanya

Chapter 2: A literal portion of Elokus from above. [73](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/1/73.aspx)
Chapter 4: The 613 limbs of the soul. [22](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/22.aspx)
In the place of His greatness, etc. [43](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/2/43.aspx)
Chapter 6: The Shechinah only rests where, etc. Even one... Shechinah... every group of ten, etc. [43](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/2/43.aspx)
All the affairs of this world are difficult... and the wicked prevail within it. [24](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/24.aspx)
And it is called in the Chariot of Yechezkel a stormy wind and a great cloud, etc. [160](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/160.aspx)
Chapter 7: This world... the majority of it is evil, etc. [24](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/24.aspx)
Chapter 8: Because of its prohibition by the Sitra Achra, etc., and even if it is a Rabbinic prohibition, which are more stringent, etc. [11](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/2/1/11.aspx)
Chapter 10: Who is a Chassid? One who acts with kindness toward his Creator, etc. [45](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/2/45.aspx)
Chapter 12: The brain rules over the heart, etc. (and notes and corrections). [101](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/3/101.aspx)
Chapter 17: A good thought, the Holy One, Blessed be He, joins it to the deed, and it should have said, etc., but, etc. [64](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/6/1/64.aspx)
Chapter 23: [Mitzvos are of the limbs, whereas Torah is higher than this]. [230](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/13/230.aspx)
[Based on "And Hashem commanded us all these statutes to fear Hashem"]. [73](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/1/73.aspx)
Chapter 25: This union above is eternal, forever and ever. [97](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/2/97.aspx)
Chapter 33: A double and redoubled joy... in the joy of Hashem... Yisrael shall rejoice in His Maker. [231](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/13/231.aspx)
Chapter 35: The concept of the resting of the Shechinah, etc., that that thing is included in the light of Hashem, etc. [44](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/2/44.aspx)
End of Chapter 36: An illumination... will illuminate the darkness of the nations, etc. [120](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/120.aspx)
Chapter 37: The ultimate perfection of the Messianic era and the resurrection of the dead depends on our deeds and our avodah throughout the duration of the exile. [100](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/8/3/100.aspx)
The soul itself requires no rectification at all, etc. [77](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/7/1/77.aspx)
Chapter 38: [The primary drawing down of mitzvos is through speech and action more than through thought]. [20](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/20.aspx)
Tefillah or any other blessing without kavanah is like a body without a soul. [52](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/1/52.aspx)
Chapter 42: Moshe Rabbeinu... is one of the seven shepherds, etc., and Moshe Rabbeinu is the inclusion of them all, etc. [193](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/5/193.aspx)
End of Chapter 49: [Regarding the teshuvah of Rabbi Elazar ben Durdaya]. [24](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/24.aspx)
Chapter 51: 613 types of powers and vitality, etc. [22](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/22.aspx)

29, 1 [During the day he would only light the western candle, etc.]: [192](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/5/192.aspx).
29, 3 That between the evenings he lights all seven candles, and in the morning, at the time of the cleaning of the two candles, etc.: [192](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/5/192.aspx).
Mitzvos that are in physical action are in the category of ketores, etc.: [185](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/185.aspx).

## לקוטי תורה

## Likutei Torah

### Vayikra
1, 1: It is not mentioned at all in the verse who the caller was [38](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/1/38.aspx).

### Kedoshim
30, 2: "And I looked, and behold, a stormy wind..." and in the holy *sefer* it is explained, etc. [160](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/160.aspx).

### Emor
36, 2: "And you shall count for yourselves from the morrow of the Shabbos, etc." — the drawing down of the *makifim* of *Imma*, etc., which are above Shabbos, etc. [144](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/2/144.aspx).

### Behar
41, 2: They occupy space... also in the aspect of time; both are created in one aspect [15](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/2/1/15.aspx).

### Bamidbar
13, 1: *Mitzvos*... the limbs of the *Melech*, etc. The Torah is the aspect of the blood... which draws the life-force into the limbs [22](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/22.aspx).

### Beha'aloscha
Beginning of the *parsha*: Aharon... is one of the seven shepherds, etc. [193](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/5/193.aspx).
30, 1: "Who is a *Chassid*? One who acts with kindness toward his Creator, etc." [45](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/2/45.aspx).

### Shelach
37, 1: They did not want to lower themselves to physical *mitzvos*, etc. [52](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/1/52.aspx).
38, 2-3: They did not want to enter *Eretz Yisrael*... physical *asiyah*... they were mistaken that the main thing is to perform them in the Land... "the land is good," etc. [52](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/5/1/52.aspx).

### Chukas
60, 1: The three *kelipos* that are impure, mentioned in the Chariot of Yechezkel: "a stormy wind, a great cloud, and a fire flashing up" [160](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/160.aspx).
65, 4: "Thick air"... in order to illuminate, etc. [185](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/185.aspx).

### Balak
70, 3-4: *Tefillah*... is not counted among the *mitzvos*... it is like the analogy of the spinal cord, etc. [22](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/22.aspx).

### Pinchas
80, 2: It is not hinted at in any letter or *kotz*, etc. [38](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/1/38.aspx).

### Masei
88, 3-89, 2: "These are the journeys"... plural form, etc. To exit the aspect of *Mitzrayim*... and therefore all the forty-two journeys, etc. [224](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/12/224.aspx).
92, 1: *Noga* is the intermediary... and this is what is stated in the Chariot of Yechezkel: "a stormy wind," etc. [160](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/160.aspx).
94, 4: "And the border shall descend"... the Torah is in measurements and boundaries, etc., and through, etc. [125](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/11/1/125.aspx).

### Va'eschanan
9, 4-10, 1: *Mitzvos*... require guarding, etc. [185](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/185.aspx).

### Re'eh
20, 1: *Mitzvos* require guarding, etc. [185](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/185.aspx).
20, 3: His *Atzmus* and *Mahus* (may He be blessed) commanded, and they were created... automatically, etc. [38](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/1/38.aspx).
32, 2: "The King... in the field," etc. He receives everyone with a smiling countenance, etc. [195](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/5/195.aspx).

### Nitzavim
44, 1: All of *Klal Yisrael* are one complete stature, as they all gather together, etc., to become unified as one [164](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/3/164.aspx).
45, 3-4: *Teshuvah*... is on a higher level than all the *mitzvos*... to fill the flaw and the deficiency, etc. [22](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/22.aspx).

### Rosh Hashanah
59, 4: It is written "He shall sound," but it is not mentioned who is doing the sounding, etc. [38](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/1/38.aspx).

### Ha'azinu
74, 4: [Regarding the *avodah* of the *Ofanim*]. [121](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/121.aspx).

### Shemini Atzeres
85, 1: *Teshuvah* and good deeds, meaning... good and illuminating, etc. [24](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/24.aspx).
91, 3: At a time when the *Beis Hamikdash* does not exist, He "peeks through the lattices," etc. [199](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/6/199.aspx).

### Beracha
97, 2: [Regarding the matter of a city-dweller and a villager]. [121](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/10/1/121.aspx).
98, 1: Space and time, both are created in one aspect [15](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/2/1/15.aspx).

### Shir HaShirim
17, 3: *Teshuvah* and good deeds... good, that they should be illuminating, etc. [24](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/3/1/24.aspx).
23, 3: "Forehead"... from the aspect of "For He is not a man," etc. [200](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/6/200.aspx).
24, 1: [Levels of *is'arusa d'lesata* and *is'arusa d'le'eila*]. [38](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/4/1/38.aspx).
48, 1-2: In the future... a new Torah... the aspect of marriage... revelation, etc. [227](@apppath/admur/lkus/38/12/12/227.aspx).
